## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task involves predicting the rate of change of concentration dA_dt from time t and concentration A, which is the core of chemical reaction rate laws. The physical relationship is typically an autonomous ordinary differential equation where dA_dt is a function of A (reaction order, saturation, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time dependence for non‑ideal or deactivating systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of A)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general reaction order, negative c1 for decay, positive for autocatalytic growth)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (approach to equilibrium, c2 is initial or total concentration)
- Autocatalytic with carrying capacity: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type self‑amplification, sigmoidal A(t))
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + c3 * A**2) (rate with high-concentration inhibition)
- Fractional order (chain reaction): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (e.g., c1 = 0.5 for radical mechanisms)
- Time‑dependent rate constant (catalyst deactivation): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A**c2 (explicit time factor)
- Power‑law time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (non‑isothermal or time‑evolving medium)
- Stretched exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (derived from Kohlrausch relaxation, dA/dt ∝ (t/τ)**(β-1) * A)
- Generalized Langmuir‑Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + c3 * A**c4 + c5 * A**c6) (complex adsorption‑kinetic control)
- Competitive inhibition analogy: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * (c3 - A)) (inhibitor expressed via initial concentration)
- Autocatalytic with general exponents: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (sigmoidal kinetics with flexible orders)
- Reversible nth-order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 + c2 * (c3 - A)**c4 (mass‑action reversible system)
- Consecutive first‑order approximation: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (intermediate concentration as explicit time function)
- Photochemical zero‑order with decay: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (light‑driven constant rate plus thermal decay)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: If dA_dt scales with A raised to a constant exponent, it suggests an elementary or pseudo‑elementary power‑law rate law.
- Explicit time dependence: Appearance of t outside A indicates time‑evolving conditions (e.g., catalyst deactivation, temperature ramps) captured by terms like exp(c*t) or t**c.
- Equilibrium approach: A difference term like (c0 - A) in dA_dt signals reversible reactions or autocatalytic saturation, leading to finite asymptotic concentration.
- Rate maximum (autocatalysis): Product form A * (c1 - A) gives a bell‑shaped rate vs. A, characteristic of autocatalytic or logistic growth.
- Saturation with inhibition: A denominator polynomial in A of degree ≥2 (e.g., c1 + c2*A + c3*A**2) implies substrate inhibition or complex multi‑site kinetics.
- Fractional exponents: Exponents like 0.5 or 1.5 are hallmarks of radical chain mechanisms with initiation‑termination balance.
- Time‑separable form: If dA_dt = f(A) * g(t), the system can be solved by separation of variables; g(t) often represents catalyst decay or external modulation.
- Constant rate term: A non‑zero constant c0 in dA_dt, independent of A, suggests zero‑order kinetics (e.g., surface saturation, photochemical rate limit).
- Combined decay sources: Sums like -c0*A - c1*A**2 indicate parallel first‑ and second‑order loss channels.
- Delayed or stretched response: Time raised to a power (t**c1) multiplied by A points to non‑exponential relaxations typical in disordered media.
